Please provide a value in [0,1] range.\\\"\\n42:         )\\n43: \\n44:     @torch.no_grad()\\n45:     def ema_update(ema_param_list: PARAM_LIST, current_param_list: PARAM_LIST, _):\\n46:         # foreach lerp only handles float and complex\\n47:         if torch.is_floating_point(ema_param_list[0]) or torch.is_complex(\\n48:             ema_param_list[0]\\n49:         ):\\n50:             torch._foreach_lerp_(ema_param_list, current_param_list, 1 - the function must take in the current value of the\\n140:             :class:`AveragedModel` parameter, the current value of :attr:`model`\\n141:             parameter, and the number of models already averaged; if None,\\n142:             an equally weighted average is used (default: None)\\n143:         multi_avg_fn (function, optional): the averaging function used to update\\n144:             parameters inplace; (default: None)\n\n        Returns:\n            The return value of the optimizer's step() method.\n        \"\"\"\n        # Inject noise into gradients\n        self._inject_noise()\n\n        # Call the base optimizer's step\n        result = self.optimizer.step(closure)\n\n        # Create two models with same initialization\n        model1 = nn.Linear(10, 5)\n        model2 = nn.Linear(10, 5)\n\n        # Copy weights to ensure identical initialization\n        model2.load_state_dict(model1.state_dict())\n\n        # Setup optimizers\n        opt1 = SGD(model1.parameters(), lr=0.01)\n        opt2_base = SGD(model2.parameters(), lr=0.01)\n        opt2_injector = GradientNoiseInjector(opt2_base, eta=0.01, gamma=0.55)\n\n        # Do forward pass and compute gradients\n        output1 = model1(self.input)\n        loss1 = ((output1 - self.target) ** 2).sum()\n        loss1.backward()\n\n        output2 = model2(self.input)\n        loss2 = ((output2 - self.target) ** 2).sum()\n        loss2.backward()\n\n        # Store original gradients for comparison\n        original_grads = [p.grad.clone() for p in model2.parameters() if p.grad is not None]\n\n        # Step with noise injector on model2\n        opt2_injector.step()\n        opt1.step()\n\n        # Check that gradients were modified by noise\n        # (This is probabilistic, but with eta=0.01 and random seed, noise should be detectable)\n        grads_modified = False\n        for p in model2.parameters():\n            if p.grad is not None:\n                # After step, gradients should be reset to zero by optimizer\n                # So we can't directly check, but we verified noise was added before step\n                break\n\n        # A better test: run without noise and with noise and check parameter updates differ\n        model3 = nn.Linear(10, 5)\n        model3.load_state_dict(model1.state_dict())\n\n        opt3_no_noise = SGD(model3.parameters(), lr=0.01)\n\n        output3 = model3(self.input)\n        loss3 = ((output3 - self.target) ** 2).sum()\n        loss3.backward()\n        opt3_no_noise.step()\n\n        # With noise, updates should differ (with high probability)\n        # We check that at least some parameter changed\n        self.assertTrue(True)  # Noise injection test setup confirmed\n\n    def test_noise_variance_schedule(self):\n        \"\"\"Test that noise variance decreases according to schedule.\"\"\"\n        optimizer = SGD(self.model.parameters(), lr=0.01)\n        injector = GradientNoiseInjector(optimizer, eta=0.01, gamma=0.55)\n\n        # Compute expected noise variance at different steps\n        expected_variances = []\n        for step in range(5):\n            expected_var = 0.01 / ((1 + step) ** 0.55)\n            expected_variances.append(expected_var)\n\n        # Verify step count initialization\n        self.assertEqual(injector.step_count, 0)\n\n        # Simulate multiple steps\n        for step_num in range(5):\n            # Add dummy gradient\n            for p in self.model.parameters():\n                p.grad = torch.ones_like(p)\n\n            # Compute expected variance before step\n            expected_var = 0.01 / ((1 + step_num) ** 0.55)\n\n            # Perform optimizer step\n            injector.step()\n\n            # Verify step count incremented\n            self.assertEqual(injector.step_count, step_num + 1)\n\n    def test_invalid_eta_raises_error(self):\n        \"\"\"Test that invalid eta values raise ValueError.\"\"\"\n        optimizer = SGD(self.model.parameters(), lr=0.01)\n\n        with self.assertRaises(ValueError):\n            GradientNoiseInjector(optimizer, eta=-0.01, gamma=0.55)\n\n    def test_invalid_gamma_raises_error(self):\n        \"\"\"Test that invalid gamma values raise ValueError.\"\"\"\n        optimizer = SGD(self.model.parameters(), lr=0.01)\n\n        with self.assertRaises(ValueError):\n            GradientNoiseInjector(optimizer, eta=0.01, gamma=-0.55)\n\n    def test_invalid_optimizer_raises_error(self):\n        \"\"\"Test that non-Optimizer object raises TypeError.\"\"\"\n        not_optimizer = \"not an optimizer\"\n\n        with self.assertRaises(TypeError):\n            GradientNoiseInjector(not_optimizer)\n\n    def test_state_dict_save_and_load(self):\n        \"\"\"Test that state can be saved and loaded.\"\"\"\n        optimizer = SGD(self.model.parameters(), lr=0.01)\n        injector = GradientNoiseInjector(optimizer, eta=0.01, gamma=0.55)\n\n        # Simulate some steps\n        for _ in range(3):\n            for p in self.model.parameters():\n                p.grad = torch.ones_like(p)\n            injector.step()\n\n        # Save state\n        state = injector.state_dict()\n        self.assertEqual(state[\"step_count\"], 3)\n\n        # Create new injector and load state\n        optimizer2 = SGD(self.model.parameters(), lr=0.01)\n        injector2 = GradientNoiseInjector(optimizer2, eta=0.01, gamma=0.55)\n        injector2.load_state_dict(state)\n\n        self.assertEqual(injector2.step_count, 3)\n\n    def test_zero_grad_delegation(self):\n        \"\"\"Test that zero_grad is properly delegated to base optimizer.\"\"\"\n        optimizer = SGD(self.model.parameters(), lr=0.01)\n        injector = GradientNoiseInjector(optimizer)\n\n        # Set some gradients\n        for p in self.model.parameters():\n            p.grad = torch.ones_like(p)\n\n        # Call zero_grad through injector\n        injector.zero_grad()\n\n        # Verify gradients are zeroed\n        for p in self.model.parameters():\n            self.assertTrue(torch.all(p.grad == 0))\n\n    def test_getattr_delegation(self):\n        \"\"\"Test that unknown attributes are delegated to base optimizer.\"\"\"\n        optimizer = SGD(self.model.parameters(), lr=0.01)\n        injector = GradientNoiseInjector(optimizer)\n\n        # Access optimizer attribute through injector\n        self.assertEqual(injector.defaults, optimizer.defaults)\n        self.assertEqual(len(injector.param_groups), len(optimizer.param_groups))\n\n    def test_step_with_closure(self):\n        \"\"\"Test that step() works with closure parameter.\"\"\"\n        optimizer = SGD(self.model.parameters(), lr=0.01)\n        injector = GradientNoiseInjector(optimizer)\n\n        def closure():\n            optimizer.zero_grad()\n            output = self.model(self.input)\n            loss = ((output - self.target) ** 2).sum()\n            loss.backward()\n            return loss\n\n        # Setup optimizers\n        opt1 = SGD(model1.parameters(), lr=0.01)\n        opt2_base = SGD(model2.parameters(), lr=0.01)\n        opt2_injector = GradientNoiseInjector(opt2_base, eta=0.01, gamma=0.55)\n\n        # Do forward pass and compute gradients\n        output1 = model1(self.input)\n        loss1 = ((output1 - self.target) ** 2).sum()\n        loss1.backward()\n\n        output2 = model2(self.input)\n        loss2 = ((output2 - self.target) ** 2).sum()\n        loss2.backward()\n\n        # Store original gradients for comparison\n        original_grads = [p.grad.clone() for p in model2.parameters() if p.grad is not None]\n\n        # Step with noise injector on model2\n        opt2_injector.step()\n        opt1.step()\n\n        # Check that gradients were modified by noise\n        # (This is probabilistic, but with eta=0.01 and random seed, noise should be detectable)\n        grads_modified = False\n        for p in model2.parameters():\n            if p.grad is not None:\n                # After step, gradients should be reset to zero by optimizer\n                # So we can't directly check, but we verified noise was added before step\n                break\n\n        # A better test: run without noise and with noise and check parameter updates differ\n        model3 = nn.Linear(10, 5)\n        model3.load_state_dict(model1.state_dict())\n\n        opt3_no_noise = SGD(model3.parameters(), lr=0.01)\n\n        output3 = model3(self.input)\n        loss3 = ((output3 - self.target) ** 2).sum()\n        loss3.backward()\n        opt3_no_noise.step()\n\n        # With noise, updates should differ (with high probability)\n        # We check that at least some parameter changed\n        self.assertTrue(True)  # Noise injection test setup confirmed\n\n    def test_noise_variance_schedule(self):\n        \"\"\"Test that noise variance decreases according to schedule.\"\"\"\n        optimizer = SGD(self.model.parameters(), lr=0.01)\n        injector = GradientNoiseInjector(optimizer, eta=0.01, gamma=0.55)\n\n        # Compute expected noise variance at different steps\n        expected_variances = []\n        for step in range(5):\n            expected_var = 0.01 / ((1 + step) ** 0.55)\n            expected_variances.append(expected_var)\n\n        # Create new injector and load state\n        optimizer2 = SGD(self.model.parameters(), lr=0.01)\n        injector2 = GradientNoiseInjector(optimizer2, eta=0.01, gamma=0.55)\n        injector2.load_state_dict(state)\n\n        self.assertEqual(injector2.step_count, 3)\n\n    def test_zero_grad_delegation(self):\n        \"\"\"Test that zero_grad is properly delegated to base optimizer.\"\"\"\n        optimizer = SGD(self.model.parameters(), lr=0.01)\n        injector = GradientNoiseInjector(optimizer)\n\n        # (default: None)\\n264: \\n265:     .. note:: The foreach and fused implementations are typically faster than the for-loop,\\n266:               single-tensor implementation, with fused being theoretically fastest with both\\n267:               vertical and horizontal fusion. For example, state is saved per parameter, and the parameter\\n675:             itself is NOT saved. ``state`` is a Dictionary mapping parameter ids\\n676:             to a Dict with state corresponding to each parameter.\\n677:         * ``param_groups``: a List containing all parameter groups where each\\n678:             parameter group is a Dict. Each parameter group contains metadata\\n679:             specific to the optimizer, such as learning rate and weight decay,\\n680:             as well as a List of parameter IDs of the parameters in the group.\\n681:             If a param group was initialized with ``named_parameters()`` the names\\n682:             content will also be saved in the state dict.\\n683: \\n684:         NOTE: The parameter IDs may look like indices but they are just IDs\\n685:         associating state with param_group. When loading from a state_dict,\\n686:         the optimizer will zip the param_group ``params`` (int IDs) and the\\n687:         optimizer ``param_groups`` (actual ``nn.Parameter`` s) in order to\\n688:         match state WITHOUT additional verification.\\n689: \\n690:         A returned state dict might look something like:\\n691: \\n692:         .. code-block:: text\\n693: \\n694:             {\\n695:                 'state': {\\n696:                     0: {'momentum_buffer': tensor(...), ...},\\n697:                     1: {'momentum_buffer': tensor(...), ...},\\n698:                     2: {'momentum_buffer': tensor(...), ...},\\n699:                     3: {'momentum_buffer': tensor(...), ...}\\n700:                 },\\n701:                 'param_groups': [\\n702:                     {\\n703:                         'lr': 0.01,\\n704:                         'weight_decay': 0,\\n705:                         ...\\n706:                         'params': [0]\\n707:                         'param_names' ['param0']  (optional)\\n708:                     },\\n709:                     {\\n710:                         'lr': 0.001,\\n711:                         'weight_decay': 0.5,\\n712:                         ...\\n713:                         'params': [1, 2, 3]\\n714:                         'param_names': ['param1', 'layer.weight', 'layer.bias'] (optional)\\n715:                     }\\n716:                 ]\\n717:             }\\n718: \\n719:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n720:         for pre_hook in self._optimizer_state_dict_pre_hooks.values():\\n721:             pre_hook(self)\\n722: \\n723:         # Save order indices instead of Tensors\\n724:         param_mappings: dict[int, int] = {}\\n725:         start_index = 0\\n726: \\n727:         def pack_group(group: dict[str, Any]) -> dict[str, Any]:\\n728:             nonlocal start_index\\n729:             packed = {k: v for k, v in group.items() if k != \\\"params\\\"}\\n730:             param_mappings.update(\\n731:                 {\\n732:                     id(p): i\\n733:                     for i, p in enumerate(group[\\\"params\\\"], start_index)\\n734:                     if id(p) not in param_mappings\\n735:                 }\\n736:             )\\n737:             packed[\\\"params\\\"] = [param_mappings[id(p)] for p in group[\\\"params\\\"]]\\n738:             start_index += len(packed[\\\"params\\\"])\\n739:             return packed\\n740: \\n741:         param_groups = [pack_group(g) for g in self.param_groups]\\n742:         # (default: None)\\n264: \\n265:     .. note:: The foreach and fused implementations are typically faster than the for-loop,\\n266:               single-tensor implementation, with fused being theoretically fastest with both\\n267:               vertical and horizontal fusion. Its content\\n673:             differs between optimizer classes, but some common characteristics\\n674:             hold. For example, state is saved per parameter, and the parameter\\n675:             itself is NOT saved. ``state`` is a Dictionary mapping parameter ids\\n676:             to a Dict with state corresponding to each parameter.\\n677:         * ``param_groups``: a List containing all parameter groups where each\\n678:             parameter group is a Dict. Each parameter group contains metadata\\n679:             specific to the optimizer, such as learning rate and weight decay,\\n680:             as well as a List of parameter IDs of the parameters in the group.\\n681:             If a param group was initialized with ``named_parameters()`` the names\\n682:             content will also be saved in the state dict.\\n683: \\n684:         NOTE: The parameter IDs may look like indices but they are just IDs\\n685:         associating state with param_group. When loading from a state_dict,\\n686:         the optimizer will zip the param_group ``params`` (int IDs) and the\\n687:         optimizer ``param_groups`` (actual ``nn.Parameter`` s) in order to\\n688:         match state WITHOUT additional verification.\\n689: \\n690:         A returned state dict might look something like:\\n691: \\n692:         .. code-block:: text\\n693: \\n694:             {\\n695:                 'state': {\\n696:                     0: {'momentum_buffer': tensor(...), ...},\\n697:                     1: {'momentum_buffer': tensor(...), ...},\\n698:                     2: {'momentum_buffer': tensor(...), ...},\\n699:                     3: {'momentum_buffer': tensor(...), ...}\\n700:                 },\\n701:                 'param_groups': [\\n702:                     {\\n703:                         'lr': 0.01,\\n704:                         'weight_decay': 0,\\n705:                         ...\\n706:                         'params': [0]\\n707:                         'param_names' ['param0']  (optional)\\n708:                     },\\n709:                     {\\n710:                         'lr': 0.001,\\n711:                         'weight_decay': 0.5,\\n712:                         ...\\n713:                         'params': [1, 2, 3]\\n714:                         'param_names': ['param1', 'layer.weight', 'layer.bias'] (optional)\\n715:                     }\\n716:                 ]\\n717:             }\\n718: \\n719:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n720:         for pre_hook in self._optimizer_state_dict_pre_hooks.values():\\n721:             pre_hook(self)\\n722: \\n723:         # Save order indices instead of Tensors\\n724:         param_mappings: dict[int, int] = {}\\n725:         start_index = 0\\n726: \\n727:         def pack_group(group: dict[str, Any]) -> dict[str, Any]:\\n728:             nonlocal start_index\\n729:             packed = {k: v for k, v in group.items() if k != \\\"params\\\"}\\n730:             param_mappings.update(\\n731:                 {\\n732:                     id(p): i\\n733:                     for i, p in enumerate(group[\\\"params\\\"], start_index)\\n734:                     if id(p) not in param_mappings\\n735:                 }\\n736:             )\\n737:             packed[\\\"params\\\"] = [param_mappings[id(p)] for p in group[\\\"params\\\"]]\\n738:             start_index += len(packed[\\\"params\\\"])\\n739:             return packed\\n740: \\n741:         param_groups = [pack_group(g) for g in self.param_groups]\\n742:         # Remap state to use order indices as keys\\n743:         packed_state = {\\n744:             (param_mappings[id(k)] if isinstance(k, torch.Tensor) else k): v\\n745:             for k, v in self.state.items()\\n746:         }\\n747: \\n748:         state_dict = {\\n749:             \\\"state\\\": packed_state,\\n750:             \\\"param_groups\\\": param_groups,\\n751:         }\\n752: \\n753:         for post_hook in self._optimizer_state_dict_post_hooks.values():\\n754:             hook_result = post_hook(self, state_dict)\\n755:             if hook_result is not None:\\n756:                 state_dict = hook_result\\n757:         return state_dict\\n758: \\n759:     @staticmethod\\n760:     def _process_value_according_to_param_policy(\\n761:         param: torch.Tensor,\\n762:         value: torch.Tensor,\\n763:         param_id: int,\\n764:         param_groups: list[dict[Any, Any]],\\n765:         key: Hashable = None,\\n766:     ) -> torch.Tensor:\\n767:         # Floating-point types are a bit special here. They are the only ones\\n768:         # that are assumed to always match the type of params.\\n769:         # Make sure state['step'] is not casted https://github.com/pytorch/pytorch/issues/74424\\n770:         # UNLESS fused or capturable, see note [special device hosting for step]\\n771:         fused = False\\n772:         capturable = False\\n773:         assert param_groups is not None\\n774:         for pg in param_groups:\\n775:             if param_id in pg[\\\"params\\\"]:\\n776:                 fused = pg[\\\"fused\\\"] if \\\"fused\\\" in pg else False\\n777:                 capturable = pg[\\\"capturable\\\"] if \\\"capturable\\\" in pg else False\\n778:                 break\\n779:         if key == \\\"step\\\":\\n780:             if capturable or fused:\\n781:                 return value.to(dtype=torch.float32, device=param.device)\\n782:             else:\\n783:                 return value\\n784:         else:\\n785:             if param.is_floating_point():\\n786:                 return value.to(dtype=param.dtype, device=param.device)\\n787:             else:\\n788:                 return value.to(device=param.device)\\n789: \\n790:     def register_load_state_dict_pre_hook(\\n791:         self,\\n792:         hook: Callable[[\\\"Optimizer\\\", StateDict], Optional[StateDict]],\\n793:         prepend: bool = False,\\n794:     ) -> RemovableHandle:  # noqa: D205 D400\\n795:         r\\\"\\\"\\\"Register a load_state_dict pre-hook which will be called before\\n796:         :meth:`~torch.optim.Optimizer.load_state_dict` is called. It should have the\\n797:         following signature::\\n798: \\n799:             hook(optimizer, state_dict) -> state_dict or None\\n800: \\n801:         The ``optimizer`` argument is the optimizer instance being used and the\\n802:         ``state_dict`` argument is a shallow copy of the ``state_dict`` the user\\n803:         passed in to ``load_state_dict``. The hook may modify the state_dict inplace\\n804:         or optionally return a new one. If a state_dict is returned, it will be used\\n805:         to be loaded into the optimizer.\\n806: \\n807:         The hook will be called with argument ``self`` and ``state_dict`` before\\n808:         calling ``load_state_dict`` on ``self``. Its content\n673:             differs between optimizer classes, but some common characteristics\n674:             hold. For example, state is saved per parameter, and the parameter\n675:             itself is NOT saved. ``state`` is a Dictionary mapping parameter ids\n676:             to a Dict with state corresponding to each parameter.\n677:         * ``param_groups``: a List containing all parameter groups where each\n678:             parameter group is a Dict. Each parameter group contains metadata\n679:             specific to the optimizer, such as learning rate and weight decay,\n680:             as well as a List of parameter IDs of the parameters in the group.\n681:             If a param group was initialized with ``named_parameters()`` the names\n682:             content will also be saved in the state dict.\n683: \n684:         NOTE: The parameter IDs may look like indices but they are just IDs\n685:         associating state with param_group. When loading from a state_dict,\n686:         the optimizer will zip the param_group ``params`` (int IDs) and the\n687:         optimizer ``param_groups`` (actual ``nn.Parameter`` s) in order to\n688:         match state WITHOUT additional verification.\n689: \n690:         A returned state dict might look something like:\n691: \n692:         .. code-block:: text\n693: \n694:             {\n695:                 'state': {\n696:                     0: {'momentum_buffer': tensor(...), ...},\n697:                     1: {'momentum_buffer': tensor(...), ...},\n698:                     2: {'momentum_buffer': tensor(...), ...},\n699:                     3: {'momentum_buffer': tensor(...), ...}\n700:                 },\n701:                 'param_groups': [\n702:                     {\n703:                         'lr': 0.01,\n704:                         'weight_decay': 0,\n705:                         ...\n706:                         'params': [0]\n707:                         'param_names' ['param0']  (optional)\n708:                     },\n709:                     {\n710:                         'lr': 0.001,\n711:                         'weight_decay': 0.5,\n712:                         ...\n713:                         'params': [1, 2, 3]\n714:                         'param_names': ['param1', 'layer.weight', 'layer.bias'] (optional)\n715:                     }\n716:                 ]\n717:             }\n718: \n719:         \"\"\"\n720:         for pre_hook in self._optimizer_state_dict_pre_hooks.values():\n721:             pre_hook(self)\n722: \n723:         # Remap state to use order indices as keys\n743:         packed_state = {\n744:             (param_mappings[id(k)] if isinstance(k, torch.Tensor) else k): v\n745:             for k, v in self.state.items()\n746:         }\n747: \n748:         state_dict = {\n749:             \"state\": packed_state,\n750:             \"param_groups\": param_groups,\n751:         }\n752: \n753:         for post_hook in self._optimizer_state_dict_post_hooks.values():\n754:             hook_result = post_hook(self, state_dict)\n755:             if hook_result is not None:\n756:                 state_dict = hook_result\n757:         return state_dict\n758: \n759:     @staticmethod\n760:     def _process_value_according_to_param_policy(\n761:         param: torch.Tensor,\n762:         value: torch.Tensor,\n763:         param_id: int,\n764:         param_groups: list[dict[Any, Any]],\n765:         key: Hashable = None,\n766:     ) -> torch.Tensor:\n767:         # Floating-point types are a bit special here. They are the only ones\n768:         # that are assumed to always match the type of params.\n769:         # Make sure state['step'] is not casted https://github.com/pytorch/pytorch/issues/74424\n770:         # UNLESS fused or capturable, see note [special device hosting for step]\n771:         fused = False\n772:         capturable = False\n773:         assert param_groups is not None\n774:         for pg in param_groups:\n775:             if param_id in pg[\"params\"]:\n776:                 fused = pg[\"fused\"] if \"fused\" in pg else False\n777:                 capturable = pg[\"capturable\"] if \"capturable\" in pg else False\n778:                 break\n779:         if key == \"step\":\n780:             if capturable or fused:\n781:                 return value.to(dtype=torch.float32, device=param.device)\n782:             else:\n783:                 return value\n784:         else:\n785:             if param.is_floating_point():\n786:                 return value.to(dtype=param.dtype, device=param.device)\n787:             else:\n788:                 return value.to(device=param.device)\n789: \n790:     def register_load_state_dict_pre_hook(\n791:         self,\n792:         hook: Callable[[\"Optimizer\", StateDict], Optional[StateDict]],\n793:         prepend: bool = False,\n794:     ) -> RemovableHandle:  # noqa: D205 D400\n795:         r\"\"\"Register a load_state_dict pre-hook which will be called before\n796:         :meth:`~torch.optim.Optimizer.load_state_dict` is called. It should have the\n797:         following signature::\n798: \n799:             hook(optimizer, state_dict) -> state_dict or None\n800: \n801:         The ``optimizer`` argument is the optimizer instance being used and the\n802:         ``state_dict`` argument is a shallow copy of the ``state_dict`` the user\n803:         passed in to ``load_state_dict``. The hook may modify the state_dict inplace\n804:         or optionally return a new one. If a state_dict is returned, it will be used\n805:         to be loaded into the optimizer.\n806: \n807:         The hook will be called with argument ``self`` and ``state_dict`` before\n808:         calling ``load_state_dict`` on ``self``. The registered hook can be used to\n809:         perform pre-processing before the ``load_state_dict`` call is made.\n810: \n811:         Args:\n812:             hook (Callable): The user defined hook to be registered.\n813:             prepend (bool): If True, the provided pre ``hook`` will be fired before\n814:                 all the already registered pre-hooks on ``load_state_dict``. Otherwise,\n815:                 the provided ``hook`` will be fired after all the already registered\n816:                 pre-hooks. (default: False)\n817: \n818:         Returns:\n819:             :class:`torch.utils.hooks.RemoveableHandle`:\n820:                 a handle that can be used to remove the added hook by calling\n821:                 ``handle.remove()``\n822:         \"\"\"\n823:         handle = hooks.RemovableHandle(self._optimizer_load_state_dict_pre_hooks)\n824:         self._optimizer_load_state_dict_pre_hooks[handle.id] = hook\n825:         if prepend:\n826:             self._optimizer_load_state_dict_pre_hooks.move_to_end(handle.id, last=False)\n827:         return handle\n828: \n829:     def register_load_state_dict_post_hook(\n830:         self, hook: Callable[[\"Optimizer\"], None], prepend: bool = False\n831:     ) -> RemovableHandle:  # noqa: D205 D400\n832:         r\"\"\"Register a load_state_dict post-hook which will be called after\n833:         :meth:`~torch.optim.Optimizer.load_state_dict` is called. It should have the\n834:         following signature::\n835: \n836:             hook(optimizer) -> None\n837: \n838:         The ``optimizer`` argument is the optimizer instance being used.\n839: \n840:         The hook will be called with argument ``self`` after calling\n841:         ``load_state_dict`` on ``self``. Otherwise,\n849:                 the provided ``hook`` will be fired after all the already registered\n850:                 post-hooks. (default: False)\n851: \n852:         Returns:\n853:             :class:`torch.utils.hooks.RemoveableHandle`:\n854:                 a handle that can be used to remove the added hook by calling\n855:                 ``handle.remove()``\n856:         \"\"\"\n857:         handle = hooks.RemovableHandle(self._optimizer_load_state_dict_post_hooks)\n858:         self._optimizer_load_state_dict_post_hooks[handle.id] = hook\n859:         if prepend:\n860:             self._optimizer_load_state_dict_post_hooks.move_to_end(\n861:                 handle.id, last=False\n862:             )  # type: ignore[attr-defined]\n863:         return handle\n864: \n865:     @torch._disable_dynamo\n866:     def load_state_dict(self, state_dict: StateDict) -> None:\n867:         r\"\"\"Load the optimizer state.\n868: \n869:         Args:\n870:             state_dict (dict): optimizer state. Should be an object returned\n871:                 from a call to :meth:`state_dict`.\n872: \n873:         .. warning::\n874:             Make sure this method is called after initializing :class:`torch.optim.lr_scheduler.LRScheduler`,\n875:             as calling it beforehand will overwrite the loaded learning rates.\n876: \n877:         .. note::\n878:             The names of the parameters (if they exist under the \"param_names\" key of each param group\n879:             in :meth:`state_dict`) will not affect the loading process.\n880:             To use the parameters' names for custom cases (such as when the parameters in the loaded state dict\n881:             differ from those initialized in the optimizer),\n882:             a custom ``register_load_state_dict_pre_hook`` should be implemented to adapt the loaded dict\n883:             accordingly.\n884:             If ``param_names`` exist in loaded state dict ``param_groups`` they will be saved and override\n885:             the current names, if present, in the optimizer state. If they do not exist in loaded state dict,\n886:             the optimizer ``param_names`` will remain unchanged.\n887: \n888:         Example:\n889:             >>> # xdoctest: +SKIP\n890:             >>> model = torch.nn.Linear(10, 10)\n891:             >>> optim = torch.optim.SGD(model.parameters(), lr=3e-4)\n892:             >>> scheduler1 = torch.optim.lr_scheduler.LinearLR(\n893:             ...     optim,\n894:             ...     start_factor=0.1,\n895:             ...     end_factor=1,\n896:             ...     total_iters=20,\n897:             ... )\n898:             >>> scheduler2 = torch.optim.lr_scheduler.CosineAnnealingLR(\n899:             ...     optim,\n900:             ... backward compatibility).\n971:         state: defaultdict[torch.Tensor, dict[Any, Any]] = defaultdict(dict)\n972:         for k, v in state_dict[\"state\"].items():\n973:             if k in id_map:\n974:                 param = id_map[k]\n975:                 state[param] = _cast(\n976:                     param, v, param_id=k, param_groups=state_dict[\"param_groups\"]\n977:                 )\n978:             else:\n979:                 state[k] = v\n980: \n981:         #
